        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have emerged in recent years, due to their advantages of natural abundance, low cost and environmental friendliness.  In this article, we review the up-to-date research progress on anode materials for Na-ion batteries from five respects: carbon-based materials, alloy-based materials, metal oxides and sulfides based on conversion reaction, titanium-based compds. with insertion mechanism, and org. composites.  In particular, we not only summarize the Na-storage mechanism of these anodes, but also discuss the failure mechanism.  The problems and challenges assocd. with these anodes are pointed out.  Furthermore, on the basis of extensive reports and our exptl. studies, feasible strategies are suggested for designing high performance anode materials.  After further in-depth exploration and investigation, we believe that Na-ion batteries are promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries for low cost and large-scale energy storage systems in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrB4Pf2vZ5QrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh7XAQUW07Qyg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFelsrnN&amp;md5=8311789a2dc4e61dabff177245235c3e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1039/C4CC09604E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A new, cheap, productive FeP anode material for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ball-milled FeP/graphite as a low-cost anode material for the sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Qiu-Ran; Li, Wei-Jie; Chou, Shu-Lei; Wang, Jia-Zhao; Liu, Hua-Kun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">98</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Phosphorus is a promising anode material for sodium batteries with a theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1.  However, phosphorus has a low elec. cond. of 1 × 10-14 S cm-1, which results in poor cycling and rate performances.  Even if it is alloyed with conductive Fe, it still delivers a poor electrochem. performance.  In this article, a FeP/graphite composite has been synthesized using a simple, cheap, and productive method of low energy ball-milling, which is an efficient way to improve the elec. cond. of the FeP compd.  The cycling performance was improved significantly, and when the c.d. increased to 500 mA g-1, the FeP/graphite composite could still deliver 134 mA h g-1, which was more than twice the capacity of the FeP compd. alone.  Our results suggest that by using a low-energy ball-milling method, a promising FeP/graphite anode material can be synthesized for the sodium battery.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrtTlXB_sD18LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh7XAQUW07Qyg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVOlsLbJ&amp;md5=ea756cb04173dee1d07c51e985623f36</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1039/C3TA13976J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fullenwarth, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Darwiche, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Soares, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Donnadieu, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Monconduit, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NiP<sub>3</sub>: a promising negative electrode for Li- and Na-ion batteries</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>2</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2050</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2059</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C3TA13976J</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D2%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D2050-2059%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DJ.%2BFullenwarth%26author%3DA.%2BDarwiche%26author%3DA.%2BSoares%26author%3DB.%2BDonnadieu%26author%3DL.%2BMonconduit%26title%3DNiP3%253A%2Ba%2Bpromising%2Bnegative%2Belectrode%2Bfor%2BLi-%2Band%2BNa-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC3TA13976J&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b00444&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC3TA13976J&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">NiP3: a promising negative electrode for Li- and Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fullenwarth, J.; Darwiche, A.; Soares, A.; Donnadieu, B.; Monconduit, L.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2050-2059</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to the abundance and low cost of sodium-contg. precursors ambient temp. sodium ion batteries are promising for large scale grid storage.  The low m.p. of Na (97.7 °C) compared to 180.6 °C for Li represents a significant safety hazard for the use of Na metal anodes at ambient temps., which emphasizes the need for scientists and engineers to identify, design and develop new neg. electrodes for Na-ion batteries.  The identification of a suitable neg. electrode is a crucial challenge for any further successful development of new cells, and to date efficient and competitive neg. electrodes for NaB are still very rare.  In this work we demonstrate that NiP3 could be a good challenger for this purpose.  NiP3 based electrodes are evaluated as neg. electrode materials for Li-ion batteries (LiB) and Na-ion batteries (NaB).  The study of the reaction mechanism reveals the formation of a phase of compn. close to Li3P and Na3P embedding Ni nanoparticles as the final reaction product after a full discharge.  While the direct conversion of NiP3 into Na3P is identified for the reaction vs. Na, it is still unclear whether an amorphous phase exists during the first discharge for the reaction vs. Li before the conversion.  Furthermore, thanks to the CM-cellulose/carbon black (CMC/CB) electrode formulation, the NiP3 electrode possesses a very promising capacity with a reversible storage capacity higher than 1000 mA h g-1 after 50 cycles for LiB and 900 mA h g-1 after 15 cycles for NaB, which represents one of the highest capacities ever sustained in Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpOUBqz1xXoSrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh7XAQUW07Qyg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXpslGjug%253D%253D&amp;md5=1e5512e9a0282ca35cdf95497825a466</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201305638"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Woo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mok, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, N. T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tin phosphide as a promising anode material for Na-ion batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                 10.1002/adma.201305638</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D26%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D4139-4144%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26author%3DY.%2BKim%26author%3DA.%2BChoi%26author%3DS.%2BWoo%26author%3DD.%2BMok%26author%3DN.%2BS.%2BChoi%26author%3DY.%2BS.%2BJung%26author%3DJ.%2BH.%2BRyu%26author%3DS.%2BM.%2BOh%26author%3DK.%2BT.%2BLee%26title%3DTin%2Bphosphide%2Bas%2Ba%2Bpromising%2Banode%2Bmaterial%2Bfor%2BNa-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.201305638&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b00444&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.201305638&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin Phosphide as a Promising Anode Material for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Youngjin; Kim, Yongil; Choi, Aram; Woo, Sangwon; Mok, Duckgyun; Choi, Nam-Soon; Jung, Yoon Seok; Ryu, Ji Heon; Oh, Seung M.; Lee, Kyu Tae</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">24</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4139-4144</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin phosphide (Sn4P3) was prepd. by ball milling of Sn and P and evaluated as a promising anode material for sodium ion batteries.  A comparison of cycle performance and voltage profiles of Sn and Sn4P3 was carried out in a half cell with a Na counter-electrode.  Both electrodes delivered a similar reversible capacity of about 718 mA-h/g when a fluoroethylene carbonate additive was used, but Sn4P3 showed a much improved cycle performance than Sn and exhibited negligible capacity fading over 100 cycles.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanostructured CuP2/C composites as high-performance anode materials for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Feipeng; Han, Na; Huang, Wenjing; Li, Jiaojiao; Ye, Hualin; Chen, Fengjiao; Li, Yanguang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Research on Na ion batteries has recently been revived.  Attention is now placed on the development of high-capacity and stable electrode materials at low costs.  Among them, compds. operating on the conversion mechanism represent a promising class of anode materials.  Unfortunately, they are generally plagued by poor elec. cond. and large vol. changes during repeated cycling.  The authors exploit a new type of composite material made of Cu phosphide and Super P C black (CuP2/C) as a potential anode candidate.  The final products consisted of cryst. CuP2 cores coated with C black nanoparticles on the surface.  Electrochem. measurements and multiple ex situ studies demonstrate that CuP2/C composites are capable of fast and reversible sodiation and desodiation based on the conversion mechanism.  They deliver a large capacity &gt;500 mA-h g-1, high rate capability and decent short-term cycling stability.  Probably these transition metal phosphides with a suitable C coating may hold great opportunities as anode materials for Na ion batteries for effective and economical energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpNvcGwcWr-prVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj7NUZOdiWh-g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsV2ltL%252FO&amp;md5=5e274a266f214959ed90f3db240495e8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1039/C5CC10585D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, S.-O.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Manthiram, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile synthesis and enhanced sodium-storage performance of chemically bonded CuP<sub>2</sub>/C hybrid anode</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polymer-Embedded Fabrication of Co2P Nanoparticles Encapsulated in N, P-Doped Graphene for Hydrogen Generation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhuang, Minghao; Ou, Xuewu; Dou, Yubing; Zhang, Lulu; Zhang, Qicheng; Wu, Ruizhe; Ding, Yao; Shao, Minhua; Luo, Zhengtang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4691-4698</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A method is developed to engineer well-distributed dicobalt phosphide (Co2P) nanoparticles encapsulated in N, P-doped graphene (Co2P@NPG) as electrocatalysts for hydrogen evolution reaction (HER).  The nanostructure is fabricated by the absorption of initiator and functional monomers, including acrylamide and phytic acid on graphene oxides, followed by UV-initiated polymn., then by adsorption of cobalt ions and finally calcination to form N, P-doped graphene structures.  The exptl. results show significantly enhanced performance for such engineered nanostructures due to the synergistic effect from nanoparticles encapsulation and nitrogen and phosphorus doping on graphene structures.  The obtained Co2P@NPG modified cathode exhibits small overpotentials of only -45 mV at 1 mA cm-2, resp., with a low Tafel slope of 58 mV dec-1 and high exchange c.d. of 0.21 mA cm-2 in 0.5 M H2SO4.  In addn., encapsulation by N, P-doped graphene effectively prevent nanoparticle from corrosion, exhibiting nearly unfading catalytic performance after 30 h testing.  This versatile method also opens a door for unprecedented design and fabrication of novel low-cost metal phosphide electrocatalysts encapsulated by graphene.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrxwtVdDkmuL7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj7NUZOdiWh-g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XpsFGls7Y%253D&amp;md5=7bb1b4cf59fb0d4b3565f00b488363b7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2017.11.006"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrospun three dimensional Co/CoP@nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers network for efficient hydrogen evolution</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">44</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">53</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Co2P/graphene nanocomposites with graphene nanosheets anchoring with Co2P nanorods are prepd. by a facile soln. method.  Their property as anode materials for lithium ion batteries is tested and compared with that of Co2P nanorods without anchoring on graphene.  Compared to Co2P counterpart, Co2P/graphene nanocomposites exhibit more enhanced performance in Li-ion reversible capacity and cycleability.  It is interesting that in both galvanostatic and rate cyclic performance, capacities show evidently increasing trend with increasing the cycle no., and then keep at an ultimate level around 800-900 mA h g-1 which is much higher than the theor. capacity of Co2P and graphene.  This enhanced property may concern with the abundant microspores in Co2P/graphene nanocomposites and the catalytic decompn. of solid electrolyte interface (SEI).  The effective combination of Co2P nanorods with graphene not only reduces the particle aggregation but also complement the limitations of Co2P as anode materials for lithium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrNQtN6aY1DwbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgWhbuV30MuAA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtF2rtrzP&amp;md5=a56247b8abbdabf7f5739791aeae9621</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1039/C3TA14430E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ho, K.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structurally tailored graphene nanosheets as lithium ion battery anodes: an insight to yield exceptionally high lithium storage performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Xifei; Hu, Yuhai; Liu, Jian; Lushington, Andrew; Li, Ruying; Sun, Xueliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">How to tune graphene nanosheets (GNSs) with various morphologies has been a significant challenge for lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  In this study, three types of GNSs with varying size, edge sites, defects and layer nos. have been successfully achieved.  It was demonstrated that controlling GNS morphol. and microstructure has important effects on its cyclic performance and rate capability in LIBs.  Diminished GNS layer no., decreased size, increased edge sites and increased defects in the GNS anode can be highly beneficial to lithium storage and result in increased electrochem. performance.  Interestingly, GNSs treated with a hydrothermal approach delivered a high reversible discharge capacity of 1348 mA h g-1.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">New insights into how RGO influences the photocatalytic performance of BiOIO3/RGO nanocomposites under visible and UV irradiation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Ting; Dong, Fan; Zhou, Ying; Fu, Min; Ho, Wing-Kei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>

        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The BiOIO3/RGO nanocomposites were prepd. by a one-pot hydrothermal method, during which BiOIO3 nanoplates were formed in situ on RGO sheets resulting from partial redn. of RGO.  The two components of the composite displayed intimate interfacial contact.  The as-prepd. BiOIO3/RGO nanocomposites exhibited highly enhanced visible photocatalytic activity, relative to that of pure BiOIO3, toward removal of NO from air.  The BiOIO3/RGO nanocomposites showed only slightly increased photocatalytic activity under UV irradn.  The limited enhancement of UV activity can be ascribed to the fact that BiOIO3 would be expected to compete with RGO with regard to absorption and utilization of UV light. Its electronic structure is captured in its Raman spectrum that clearly evolves with the no. of layers.  The D peak 2nd order changes in shape, width, and position for an increasing no. of layers, reflecting the change in the electron bands via a double resonant Raman process.  The G peak slightly down-shifts.  This allows unambiguous, high-throughput, nondestructive identification of graphene layers, which is critically lacking in this emerging research area.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo35CDycv0LILVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljMg550dGUYHA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD28XhtFKqtbvP&amp;md5=8b1d9f77f616aea008d55ba4fbb3f0bb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2014.05.063"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Z.-G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.-B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dasari, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Z.-Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Three dimensional graphene aerogels and their electrically conductive composites</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>77</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">592</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">599</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tailored lithium storage performance of graphene aerogel anodes with controlled surface defects for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shan, Hui; Xiong, Dongbin; Li, Xifei; Sun, Yipeng; Yan, Bo; Li, Dejun; Lawes, Stephen; Cui, Yanhua; Sun, Xueliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Surface Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Three dimensional self-assembled graphene aerogel (GA) anode materials with some surface defects have been successfully generated through a facile hydrothermal procedure using graphene oxide as precursor.  The morphologies and textural properties of as-obtained GA were investigated by SEM, transmission electron microscopy, XPS, Raman, and other spectroscopy techniques.  The surface defects and elec. conductivities of GA can be controlled by adjusting the hydrothermal reaction time.  The results indicate that GA with a reaction time of 6 h exhibits extremely high reversible capacity (1430 mAh g-1 at the c.d. of 100 mA g-1) and superior rate capability (587 mAh g-1 at 800 mA g-1) with excellent cycling stability (maintaining a reversible capacity of 960 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles).         </div><div class="casAbstract">The Sn-based materials have been hindered from practical use for lithium ion batteries due to the inherent vol. change leading to poor cycling performance.  To mitigate this challenge, in this study, amorphous SnO2/graphene aerogel nanocomposites are fabricated via a simple hydrothermal approach.  The amorphous nature of SnO2 is clearly detd. in detail by transmission electron microscopy, aberration-cor. scanning transmission electron microscopy, and X-ray diffraction measurement.  The as-prepd. material shows satisfying reversible capacity and significant cyclic stability.  For instance, it delivers an excellent discharge capacity of 700.1 mA h g-1 in 80th cycle at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1, in accordance with a high retention capacity of 97.6% compared to that of the sixth cycles, which is much better than cryst. SnO2/graphene aerogel. The resulting material of well-defined mesoporosity and a high sp. surface area (148 m2 g-1) can be directly employed as a bifunctional and flexible working electrode for both hydrogen and oxygen evolution reactions, showing superior activities as compared with noble metal benchmarks and state-of-the-art transition-metal-based catalysts.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal-organic frameworks derived porous core/shellCoP@C polyhedrons anchored on 3D reduced graphene oxide networks as anode for sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ge, Xiaoli; Li, Zhaoqiang; Yin, Longwei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel strategy is developed to synthesize metal-org. framework (MOF) derived core/shell structured CoP@C polyhedrons anchored on 3D reduced grapheme oxide (RGO) on nickel foam (NF) as binder-free anode for high performance sodium-ion battery, through an in-situ low-temp. phosphidation process from ZIF-67 derived core/shell Co@C polyhedral structures.  The unique CoP@C-RGO-NF binder-free anode exhibits a remarkable electrochem. performance with outstanding cycling stability and high rate capability, delivering a specific capacity of 473.1 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles.  The excellent properties can be attributed to synergistic effects between core/shell CoP@C polyhedrons and RGO networks.  The unique core/shell CoP@C polyhedrons can offer more electrode/electrolyte contact area and reduce the diffusion distance of Na+, while carbon layer shell can enhance electronic cond. and buffer vol. change, and prevent CoP from pulverization and aggregation.  Furthermore, 3D RGO networks can provide adequate surface areas for a high loading content of CoP and enhance charge transfer kinetics.  Meanwhile, RGO/NF can efficiently act as a binder and elec. conductor to interconnect the sep. CoP@C polyhedrons.  The present strategy for CoP@C-RGO-NF architectures can be extended to other novel electrodes for high performance energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoEA0RBe_Ev_LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lijRyxinC06_A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitFGiurfO&amp;md5=95bf6b3529a8069bf6929d1f00eeaf34</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1002/ange.201209689"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Capacity and Rate Capability of Amorphous Phosphorus for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew.                         "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.5b00376"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liou, Sz</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Red phosphorus single-walled carbon nanotube composite as a superior anode for sodium ion batteries</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>9</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3254</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3264</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsnano.5b00376</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D9%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D3254-3264%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DY.%2BZhu%26author%3DY.%2BWen%26author%3DX.%2BFan%26author%3DT.%2BGao%26author%3DF.%2BHan%26author%3DC.%2BLuo%26author%3DSz%2BLiou%26author%3DC.%2BWang%26title%3DRed%2Bphosphorus%2Bsingle-walled%2Bcarbon%2Bnanotube%2Bcomposite%2Bas%2Ba%2Bsuperior%2Banode%2Bfor%2Bsodium%2Bion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.5b00376&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b00444&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.5b00376&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Red Phosphorus-Single-Walled Carbon Nanotube Composite as a Superior Anode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Yujie; Wen, Yang; Fan, Xiulin; Gao, Tao; Han, Fudong; Luo, Chao; Liou, Sz-Chian; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3254-3264</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered as a top alternative to Li ion batteries due to the earth abundance and low cost of Na compared with Li.  Among all proposed anode materials for SIBs, red P is a very promising candidate because it has the highest theor. capacity (∼2600 mA-h g-1).  A red P-single-walled C nanotube (denoted as red P-SWCNT) composite, in which red P is uniformly distributed between tangled SWCNTs bundles, is fabricated by a modified vaporization-condensation method.  Benefiting from the nondestructive prepn. process, the highly conductive and mech. strong SWCNT network is preserved, which enhances the cond. of the composite and stabilizes the solid electrolyte interphase.  As a result, the red P-SWCNT composite presents a high overall Na storage capacity (∼700 mA-h g-1composite at 50 mA/gcomposite), fast rate capability (∼300 mA-h g-1composite at 2000 mA/gcomposite), and stable long-term cycling performance with 80% capacity retention after 2000 sodiation-desodiation cycles.  The red P-SWCNT composite fabricated by the vaporization-condensation method significantly extends the cycling stability of P/C composite from current ∼100 cycles to ∼2000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqd3GxgIxmfmbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lijRyxinC06_A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXjvVOhs7c%253D&amp;md5=6ba87307633bf69051e0eb4e034c85a8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1021/nl203967r"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Carney, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Engineering Empty Space between Si Nanoparticles for Lithium-Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">904</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">909</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/nl203967r</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D12%26publication_year%3D2012%26pages%3D904-909%26journal%3DNano%2BLett.%26author%3DH.%2BWu%26author%3DG.%2BZheng%26author%3DN.%2BLiu%26author%3DT.%2BCarney%26author%3DY.%2BYang%26author%3DY.%2BCui%26title%3DEngineering%2BEmpty%2BSpace%2Bbetween%2BSi%2BNanoparticles%2Bfor%2BLithium-Ion%2BBattery%2BAnodes%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fnl203967r&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b00444&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fnl203967r&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Engineering Empty Space between Si Nanoparticles for Lithium-Ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Hui; Zheng, Guangyuan; Liu, Nian; Carney, Thomas J.; Yang, Yuan; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">904-909</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Si is a promising high-capacity anode material for Li-ion batteries yet attaining long cycle life remains a challenge due to pulverization of the Si and unstable solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) formation during electrochem. cycling.  Despite advances in nanostructured Si electrodes, challenges including short cycle life and scalability hinder its implementation.  To address these challenges, the authors engineered an empty space between Si nanoparticles by encapsulating them in hollow C tubes.  The synthesis process used low-cost Si nanoparticles and electrospinning methods, both of which can be easily scaled.  The empty space around the Si nanoparticles allowed the electrode to overcome these problems the anode demonstrated a high gravimetric capacity (∼1000 mA-h/g based on the total mass) and long cycle life (200 cycles with 90% capacity retention).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrW7SuDc3SFW7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lijRyxinC06_A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XktVCquw%253D%253D&amp;md5=769e0fea3bde989f0adc68de9038d26f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1007/s10800-016-0961-1"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Carbon nanotubes cross-linked Zn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub> nanoparticles/graphene networks as high capacities, long life anode materials for lithium ion batteries</span>. <i>J. Appl. Electrochem.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>46</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">851</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">860</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1007/s10800-016-0961-1</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D46%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D851-860%26journal%3DJ.%2BAppl.%2BElectrochem.%26author%3DH.%2BShan%26author%3DY.%2BZhao%26author%3DX.%2BLi%26author%3DD.%2BXiong%26author%3DL.%2BDong%26author%3DB.%2BYan%26author%3DD.%2BLi%26author%3DX.%2BSun%26title%3DCarbon%2Bnanotubes%2Bcross-linked%2BZn2SnO4%2Bnanoparticles%252Fgraphene%2Bnetworks%2Bas%2Bhigh%2Bcapacities%252C%2Blong%2Blife%2Banode%2Bmaterials%2Bfor%2Blithium%2Bion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1007%252Fs10800-016-0961-1&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b00444&amp;doiOfLink=10.1007%2Fs10800-016-0961-1&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon nanotubes cross-linked Zn2SnO4 nanoparticles/graphene networks as high capacities, long life anode materials for lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shan, Hui; Zhao, Yang; Li, Xifei; Xiong, Dongbin; Dong, Lei; Yan, Bo; Li, Dejun; Sun, Xueliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Applied Electrochemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">46</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">851-860</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JAELBJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0021-891X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">By shielding zinc stannate (ZTO, viz., Zn2SnO4) nanoparticles with reduced graphene oxide (RGO) as well as multi-wall carbon nanotubes (MWCNTs), we have successfully created ZTO/RGO/MWCNTs composites via a facile hydrothermal process.  In the designed hybrid nanostructure, acting as the strut and bridge to open the graphene sheets, 3D RGO/MWCNT nets not only tackle the problem of vol. expansion and the aggregation of ZTO nanoparticles, but also maintain the integration of anode materials for high electrochem. performance.  As a result, the resultant anode material shows high reversible capacity, superior rate capacity and long-running cycle performance for lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  For instance, a excellent reversible capacity of 915.9 mAh g-1 was obtained at the c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 340 cycles.  Our study demonstrates significant potential of ZTO/RGO/MWCNTs as anode materials for LIBs.  Graphical Abstr.: [Figure not available: see fulltext.].</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqfo5L9IwKtGLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lghxQbVATvbwQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XmvFOqtr8%253D&amp;md5=3724063e6d963f1c83e48eef20df3995</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2017.05.046"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An advanced CoSe embedded within porous carbon polyhedra hybrid for high performance lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Chem. Eng. J.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>325</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">14</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">24</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.cej.2017.05.046</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D325%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D14-24%26journal%3DChem.%2BEng.%2BJ.%26author%3DJ.%2BLi%26author%3DD.%2BYan%26author%3DT.%2BLu%26author%3DY.%2BYao%26author%3DL.%2BPan%26title%3DAn%2Badvanced%2BCoSe%2Bembedded%2Bwithin%2Bporous%2Bcarbon%2Bpolyhedra%2Bhybrid%2Bfor%2Bhigh%2Bperformance%2Blithium-ion%2Band%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.cej.2017.05.046&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b00444&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.cej.2017.05.046&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An advanced CoSe embedded within porous carbon polyhedra hybrid for high performance lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Jiabao; Yan, Dong; Lu, Ting; Yao, Yefeng; Pan, Likun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">325</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14-24</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel composite contg. CoSe and porous carbon polyhedra (PCP), denoted as CoSe@PCP, was successfully synthesized using Co-based zeolitic imidazolate framework (ZIF-67) as precursor through a two-step method, including carbonization of ZIF-67 and subsequent selenization.  The field-emission SEM and transmission electron microscopy characterizations confirm that CoSe nanoparticles are uniformly dispersed in PCP.  When the CoSe@PCP was used as anode material for lithium-ion batteries, it exhibits superior performance with a high reversible capacity of 675 mAh g-1 at 200 mA g-1 after 100 cycles and 708.2 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 500 cycles as well as excellent cycling stability.  Addnl., the CoSe@PCP also demonstrates excellent performance as anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  A reversible capacity of 341 mAh g-1 can be obtained over 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1 with high cycling stability.  The excellent battery performance of CoSe@PCP should be attributed to the synergistic effect of nanostructured CoSe and PCP derived from ZIF-67, in which the nanostructured CoSe possesses high reactivity towards lithium and sodium ions and the PCP can provide a continuous conductive matrix to facilitate the charge transfer and an effective buffering to mitigate the structure variation of CoSe during cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp4EHDoBUtGbrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lghxQbVATvbwQ"> &gt;&gt; Francis; Leifer, Nicole; Jacob, David; Aurbach, Doron</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),

        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">27</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Presented herein is a discussion of the forefront in research and development of advanced electrode materials and electrolyte solns. for the next generation of lithium ion batteries.  The main challenge of the field today is in meeting the demands necessary to make the elec. vehicle fully com. viable.  This requires high energy and power densities with no compromise in safety.  Three families of advanced cathode materials (the limiting factor for energy d. in the Li battery systems) are discussed in detail: LiMn1.5Ni0.5O4 high voltage spinel compds., Li2MnO3-LiMO2 high capacity composite layered compds., and LiMPO4, where M = Fe, Mn.  Graphite, Si, LixTOy, and MO (conversion reactions) are discussed as anode materials.  The electrolyte is a key component that dets. the ability to use high voltage cathodes and low voltage anodes in the same system.  Electrode-soln. interactions and passivation phenomena on both electrodes in Li-ion batteries also play significant roles in detg. stability, cycle life and safety features.  This presentation is aimed at providing an overall picture of the road map necessary for the future development of advanced high energy d. Li-ion batteries for EV applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrHG44yQ70js7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljD1IUuRX5uFw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXotFSnurc%253D&amp;md5=080369f3bd98476b8bd50a778dae733f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201502057"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lawes, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Controlled SnO<sub>2</sub> crystallinity effectively dominating sodium storage performance</span>. <i>Adv. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">17899</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">17913</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C5TA03181H</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Update on anode materials for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kang, Hongyan; Liu, Yongchang; Cao, Kangzhe; Zhao, Yan; Jiao, Lifang; Wang, Yijing; Yuan, Huatang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">35</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">17899-17913</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have emerged in recent years, due to their advantages of natural abundance, low cost and environmental friendliness.  In this article, we review the up-to-date research progress on anode materials for Na-ion batteries from five respects: carbon-based materials, alloy-based materials, metal oxides and sulfides based on conversion reaction, titanium-based compds. with insertion mechanism, and org. composites.  In particular, we not only summarize the Na-storage mechanism of these anodes, but also discuss the failure mechanism.  The problems and challenges assocd. with these anodes are pointed out.  Furthermore, on the basis of extensive reports and our exptl. studies, feasible strategies are suggested for designing high performance anode materials.  After further in-depth exploration and investigation, we believe that Na-ion batteries are promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries for low cost and large-scale energy storage systems in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrB4Pf2vZ5QrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljD1IUuRX5uFw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFelsrnN&amp;md5=8311789a2dc4e61dabff177245235c3e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1039/C4CC09604E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A new, cheap, productive FeP anode material for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Chem. Commun.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>51</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3682</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3685</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Phosphorus is a promising anode material for sodium batteries with a theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1.  However, phosphorus has a low elec. cond. of 1 × 10-14 S cm-1, which results in poor cycling and rate performances.  Even if it is alloyed with conductive Fe, it still delivers a poor electrochem. performance.  In this article, a FeP/graphite composite has been synthesized using a simple, cheap, and productive method of low energy ball-milling, which is an efficient way to improve the elec. cond. of the FeP compd.  The cycling performance was improved significantly, and when the c.d. increased to 500 mA g-1, the FeP/graphite composite could still deliver 134 mA h g-1, which was more than twice the capacity of the FeP compd. alone.  Our results suggest that by using a low-energy ball-milling method, a promising FeP/graphite anode material can be synthesized for the sodium battery.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrtTlXB_sD18LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljD1IUuRX5uFw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVOlsLbJ&amp;md5=ea756cb04173dee1d07c51e985623f36</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1039/C3TA13976J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fullenwarth, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Darwiche, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Soares, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Donnadieu, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Monconduit, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NiP<sub>3</sub>: a promising negative electrode for Li- and Na-ion batteries</span>. <i>J.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to the abundance and low cost of sodium-contg. precursors ambient temp. sodium ion batteries are promising for large scale grid storage.  The low m.p. of Na (97.7 °C) compared to 180.6 °C for Li represents a significant safety hazard for the use of Na metal anodes at ambient temps., which emphasizes the need for scientists and engineers to identify, design and develop new neg. electrodes for Na-ion batteries.  The identification of a suitable neg. electrode is a crucial challenge for any further successful development of new cells, and to date efficient and competitive neg. electrodes for NaB are still very rare.  In this work we demonstrate that NiP3 could be a good challenger for this purpose.  NiP3 based electrodes are evaluated as neg. electrode materials for Li-ion batteries (LiB) and Na-ion batteries (NaB).  The study of the reaction mechanism reveals the formation of a phase of compn. close to Li3P and Na3P embedding Ni nanoparticles as the final reaction product after a full discharge.  While the direct conversion of NiP3 into Na3P is identified for the reaction vs. Na, it is still unclear whether an amorphous phase exists during the first discharge for the reaction vs. Li before the conversion.  Furthermore, thanks to the CM-cellulose/carbon black (CMC/CB) electrode formulation, the NiP3 electrode possesses a very promising capacity with a reversible storage capacity higher than 1000 mA h g-1 after 50 cycles for LiB and 900 mA h g-1 after 15 cycles for NaB, which represents one of the highest capacities ever sustained in Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpOUBqz1xXoSrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8uClaEFN7yQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXpslGjug%253D%253D&amp;md5=1e5512e9a0282ca35cdf95497825a466</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref8" class="rightTabRefNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit8" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201305638"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Woo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mok, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, N.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Research on Na ion batteries has recently been revived.  Attention is now placed on the development of high-capacity and stable electrode materials at low costs.  Among them, compds. operating on the conversion mechanism represent a promising class of anode materials.  Unfortunately, they are generally plagued by poor elec. cond. and large vol. changes during repeated cycling.  The authors exploit a new type of composite material made of Cu phosphide and Super P C black (CuP2/C) as a potential anode candidate.  The final products consisted of cryst.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A method is developed to engineer well-distributed dicobalt phosphide (Co2P) nanoparticles encapsulated in N, P-doped graphene (Co2P@NPG) as electrocatalysts for hydrogen evolution reaction (HER).  The nanostructure is fabricated by the absorption of initiator and functional monomers, including acrylamide and phytic acid on graphene oxides, followed by UV-initiated polymn., then by adsorption of cobalt ions and finally calcination to form N, P-doped graphene structures. The obtained Co2P@NPG modified cathode exhibits small overpotentials of only -45 mV at 1 mA cm-2, resp., with a low Tafel slope of 58 mV dec-1 and high exchange c.d. of 0.21 mA cm-2 in 0.5 M H2SO4.  In addn., encapsulation by N, P-doped graphene effectively prevent nanoparticle from corrosion, exhibiting nearly unfading catalytic performance after 30 h testing.  This versatile method also opens a door for unprecedented design and fabrication of novel low-cost metal phosphide electrocatalysts encapsulated by graphene.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrxwtVdDkmuL7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgXELHU5Z720w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XpsFGls7Y%253D&amp;md5=7bb1b4cf59fb0d4b3565f00b488363b7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2017.11.006"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrospun three dimensional Co/CoP@nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers network for efficient hydrogen evolution</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">44</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">53</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

Compared to Co2P counterpart, Co2P/graphene nanocomposites exhibit more enhanced performance in Li-ion reversible capacity and cycleability. It was demonstrated that controlling GNS morphol. and microstructure has important effects on its cyclic performance and rate capability in LIBs. The BiOIO3/RGO nanocomposites showed only slightly increased photocatalytic activity under UV irradn. Evidence shows that RGO can act as a semiconductor rather than a photosensitizer or electron reservoir in BiOIO3/RGO nanocomposites.  The active species responsible for photoactivity were investigated by a DMPO spin-trapping ESR technique.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene is the 2-dimensional building block for C allotropes of every other dimensionality.  Its electronic structure is captured in its Raman spectrum that clearly evolves with the no. of layers.  The D peak 2nd order changes in shape, width, and position for an increasing no. of layers, reflecting the change in the electron bands via a double resonant Raman process.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Three dimensional self-assembled graphene aerogel (GA) anode materials with some surface defects have been successfully generated through a facile hydrothermal procedure using graphene oxide as precursor.  The morphologies and textural properties of as-obtained GA were investigated by SEM, transmission electron microscopy, XPS, Raman, and other spectroscopy techniques.  The surface defects and elec. conductivities of GA can be controlled by adjusting the hydrothermal reaction time.  The results indicate that GA with a reaction time of 6 h exhibits extremely high reversible capacity (1430 mAh g-1 at the c.d. of 100 mA g-1) and superior rate capability (587 mAh g-1 at 800 mA g-1) with excellent cycling stability (maintaining a reversible capacity of 960 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles).             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel strategy is developed to synthesize metal-org. framework (MOF) derived core/shell structured CoP@C polyhedrons anchored on 3D reduced grapheme oxide (RGO) on nickel foam (NF) as binder-free anode for high performance sodium-ion battery, through an in-situ low-temp. phosphidation process from ZIF-67 derived core/shell Co@C polyhedral structures.  The unique CoP@C-RGO-NF binder-free anode exhibits a remarkable electrochem. performance with outstanding cycling stability and high rate capability, delivering a specific capacity of 473.1 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles.  The excellent properties can be attributed to synergistic effects between core/shell CoP@C polyhedrons and RGO networks.  The unique core/shell CoP@C polyhedrons can offer more electrode/electrolyte contact area and reduce the diffusion distance of Na+, while carbon layer shell can enhance electronic cond. and buffer vol. change, and prevent CoP from pulverization and aggregation.  Furthermore, 3D RGO networks can provide adequate surface areas for a high loading content of CoP and enhance charge transfer kinetics.  Meanwhile, RGO/NF can efficiently act as a binder and elec. conductor to interconnect the sep. CoP@C polyhedrons.  The present strategy for CoP@C-RGO-NF architectures can be extended to other novel electrodes for high performance energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoEA0RBe_Ev_LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhFQcDhL8eSPw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitFGiurfO&amp;md5=95bf6b3529a8069bf6929d1f00eeaf34</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref35" class="rightTabRefNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit35" data-doi="10.1002/ange.201209689"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Capacity and Rate Capability of Amorphous Phosphorus for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew.                         rightTab-cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Red Phosphorus-Single-Walled Carbon Nanotube Composite as a Superior Anode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Yujie; Wen, Yang; Fan, Xiulin; Gao, Tao; Han, Fudong; Luo, Chao; Liou, Sz-Chian; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered as a top alternative to Li ion batteries due to the earth abundance and low cost of Na compared with Li.  Among all proposed anode materials for SIBs, red P is a very promising candidate because it has the highest theor. capacity (∼2600 mA-h g-1).  A red P-single-walled C nanotube (denoted as red P-SWCNT) composite, in which red P is uniformly distributed between tangled SWCNTs bundles, is fabricated by a modified vaporization-condensation method.  Benefiting from the nondestructive prepn. process, the highly conductive and mech. strong SWCNT network is preserved, which enhances the cond. of the composite and stabilizes the solid electrolyte interphase.  As a result, the red P-SWCNT composite presents a high overall Na storage capacity (∼700 mA-h g-1composite at 50 mA/gcomposite), fast rate capability (∼300 mA-h g-1composite at 2000 mA/gcomposite), and stable long-term cycling performance with 80% capacity retention after 2000 sodiation-desodiation cycles.  The red P-SWCNT composite fabricated by the vaporization-condensation method significantly extends the cycling stability of P/C composite from current ∼100 cycles to ∼2000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqd3GxgIxmfmbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhFQcDhL8eSPw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXjvVOhs7c%253D&amp;md5=6ba87307633bf69051e0eb4e034c85a8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1021/nl203967r"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Carney, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Engineering Empty Space between Si Nanoparticles for Lithium-Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">904</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">909</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Si is a promising high-capacity anode material for Li-ion batteries yet attaining long cycle life remains a challenge due to pulverization of the Si and unstable solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) formation during electrochem. cycling.  Despite advances in nanostructured Si electrodes, challenges including short cycle life and scalability hinder its implementation.  To address these challenges, the authors engineered an empty space between Si nanoparticles by encapsulating them in hollow C tubes.  The synthesis process used low-cost Si nanoparticles and electrospinning methods, both of which can be easily scaled.  The empty space around the Si nanoparticles allowed the electrode to overcome these problems the anode demonstrated a high gravimetric capacity (∼1000 mA-h/g based on the total mass) and long cycle life (200 cycles with 90% capacity retention).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrW7SuDc3SFW7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhFQcDhL8eSPw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XktVCquw%253D%253D&amp;md5=769e0fea3bde989f0adc68de9038d26f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref39" class="rightTabRefNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit39" data-doi="10.1007/s10800-016-0961-1"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Carbon nanotubes cross-linked Zn<sub>2</sub>SnO<sub>4</sub> nanoparticles/graphene networks as high capacities, long life anode materials for lithium ion batteries</span>. <i>J.                         rightTab-cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon nanotubes cross-linked Zn2SnO4 nanoparticles/graphene networks as high capacities, long life anode materials for lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shan, Hui; Zhao, Yang; Li, Xifei; Xiong, Dongbin; Dong, Lei; Yan, Bo; Li, Dejun; Sun, Xueliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Applied Electrochemistry</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">By shielding zinc stannate (ZTO, viz., Zn2SnO4) nanoparticles with reduced graphene oxide (RGO) as well as multi-wall carbon nanotubes (MWCNTs), we have successfully created ZTO/RGO/MWCNTs composites via a facile hydrothermal process.  In the designed hybrid nanostructure, acting as the strut and bridge to open the graphene sheets, 3D RGO/MWCNT nets not only tackle the problem of vol. expansion and the aggregation of ZTO nanoparticles, but also maintain the integration of anode materials for high electrochem. performance.  As a result, the resultant anode material shows high reversible capacity, superior rate capacity and long-running cycle performance for lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  For instance, a excellent reversible capacity of 915.9 mAh g-1 was obtained at the c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 340 cycles.  Our study demonstrates significant potential of ZTO/RGO/MWCNTs as anode materials for LIBs.                         rightTab-cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An advanced CoSe embedded within porous carbon polyhedra hybrid for high performance lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Jiabao; Yan, Dong; Lu, Ting; Yao, Yefeng; Pan, Likun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
